- 8 2-                        ANNEX II
Page 1 of 3
KENYA NATIONAL AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH PROJECT
ORGANIZATION, MANAGEMENT. MONITORING AND EVALUATION;
JOB DESCRIPTIONS OF KEY KARI STAFF
Introduction
1.       This Annex deals with some organization and management aspects of
the new KARI. Specifically, it discusses proposals fors
(i)     reorganizing KARI, the research centers and research;
(ii)    responsibilities assigned to the Board of Management;
(iii)   planning and programming of research; and
(iv)    supervision, monitoring and evaluation of research and
scientists.
The new Kenya Agricultural Research Inccixute
2.       The new Kenya Agricultural Researeh Institute would be a semi-
autonomous Government agency which consolidlates the existing KARI at
Muguga, the Scientific Research Divisi3v of MOA and the Veterinary Research
Division of MOLD, into the reorganized Kenya Agricultural Research
Institute at Nairobi. Existing legislation, the (amended) Science and
Technology Act of 1977, established the basis for KARI as well as for
Research Institutes in other fields. Several other Research Institutes
were established and function well. The Kenya Medical Research Institute
for example is a model of an effective research establishment. The Kenya
Agricultural Research Institute was never established as provided for under
the Act. What has been called KARI was merely one research station located
at Muguga which was formerly the headquarters of the East African
Community's Agricultural Research Organization. The organization and
management systems for the new KARI would be partly modelled on those
successfully introduced by the Kenya Medical Research Institute since they
are judged conducive .o the production of high quality and valuable
research. No new legislation is required.
3.       The organigram of KARI, shown in Chart 1, provides for a Board of
Management, a Director, and three Departments, each headed by a Deputy
Director (Crops, Soils and Water; Livestock; and Finance, Planning, Finance
and Administration). All crop and proakuction factor oriented stations
would be under the authority of the Deputy Director for Crops, Soils and
Water who would be aided by Assistant Directors for: Soil, Water and other
Resources; Crops; and Regional Research Centers. The Deputy Director for
Livestock would supervise all animal production and animal health research
with Assistant Directors for: Animal Health; and Animal Production. An
internal Auditor would report directly to the Managing Director. The
external audit of KARI would be undertaken by Kenya's Auditor General
Corporations. The Chairman of the Board of Management was nominated by the
Minister of Agriculture in November 1986, and his nomination was approved
by Kenya's President. Other members of the Board have been appointed and
include representatives of Nairobi University, private enterprise and high



- 83 -                         ANNEX II
Page 2 of 3
level civil servants from MRST and also the Ministries of Agriculture,
Livestock Development, Finance and Planning. This organization is
consistent with KARI's status and with the requirements of the Science and
Technology Act. The Board would meet at least four times per year. KARI's
Managing Director is Secretary to the Board and to the Board's twfo standing
committees: the Finance and Administration Committee, and the Science and
Technical Committee. The Board will deliberate on policy issues. The
Board would also be a mechanism for coordinating input into agricultural
research policy by those ministries and non-Government institutions
interested in the results of research. The Board of Management has
delegated adequate powers to the Director of KARI, consistent with the
legislation defining the role of managers and Boards of Directors of state
corporations in Kenya (outlined in the State Corporations Act of November
1986). Therefore, day to day management would be the responsibility of
KARI management staff. The establishment of effective management functions,
particularly research planning, programming, budgeting, supervision,
reporting, monitoring and evaluation would be critical to the success of
the national agricultural research program.
4.       The establishment of the new KARI began in November 1986 and it is
envisaged that the KARI organization and management systems will be
functional by July 1, 1987. However, another year will be required for
full development of cost accounting, monitoring and evaluation, and
financial management systems. Draft job descriptiorLs for key KARI
management staff are provided in Appendix 1. These would be finalized and
approved by the KARI Board before the end of 1987. The most essential task
of KARI's management is the timely implementation of the NARP.
5.       Under the amended Science and Technology Act and the State
Corporations Act of 1986, KARI is empowered to enter into contracts with
third parties, to procure goods and services both nationally and
internationally and to sell produce (from research stations). KAR, can
acquire and hold property on its own name, and can sue or be sued in its
corporate name.
Adaptive Research at Regional Research Centers
6.       Each of the RRCs (Table 1) would focus on the identification and
diagnosis of production problems in its assigned agro-ecological zone and
adapt technologies for increasing production at the farm level. The
Regional Research Centers would include Mtwapa, Embu, Garissa, Kakamega,
Njoro, Katumani, Kitale and Kisii. Regional research on extensive
livestock production would also be carried out at Kiboko and Marsabit
(Table 1). A proposed organigram for a research center is shown in Chart
2.
Improved National Commodity and Factor Research Programs
7.       Nationally coordinated commodity and factor research programs
would initially be organized out of 16 National Research Centers, and two
Regional Research Centers. The National Research Centers with their
corresponding commodity and factor programs are listed in Table 2. For



- 84-                        ANNEX II
Pase 3 of 3
several of these programs further work is required to determine the
appropriate center in which to place the lead responsibility and
coordinating role (e.g. plant protection, cotton, sorghum/millet,
pasture/fodder and livestock). NRCs will address national research
problems of commodities or factors of production. They will be the
principal research stations for generating and testing improved
technologies, e.g. for maize, wheat, veterinary medicine, oilseeds, and
soil and water management. NRCs vould be organized and managed in a manner
defined by their long-term strategic plans that are presently being
prepared. Models have been completed for programs at the Kitale, Muguga
and Katumani NRCs.
Research Planning and Programming
8.       KARI's budget cycle has to be tied with GOK's financial year.  For
budget purposes, the annual research programming exercise would begin at
the end of June when NRCs, RRCs and commodity and factor coordinators
submit their annual reports for the previous year and initial proposals for
the coming 3 years to KARI's Planning, Programming and Budgeting Section.
The coming year begins July 1 of the next year.   A meeting on June 30,
1987 for example will plan for the budget year July 1, 1988 to June 30,
1989. After many modifications, the exercise ends in early April when the
final Annual Plan and Budget are communicated to Research Centers for use
in the year beginning July 1. However, the research planning sequence at
crops research centers is determined not by the fiscal year but by the
beginning and end of the growing season. Thus, planning of any year's
annual program needs to start more than 1 year before the start of a given
season, while adjustments to the current year's program are made on the
basis of preliminary budget dat&. A detailed research programming calendar
is given in Table 3.
Supervision, Monitoring and Evaluation
9.       Supervisory roles are explicit in the organization proposed for
KARI (see Chart 1) and in the job descriptions of key KARI staff (Appendix
1). Under the National Agriculture Research Program, a monitoring and
evaluation (M & E) system will be established to ensure that research is
steered in the proper direction and that the scarce resources available are
allocated according to priorities and effectively utilized. The Monitoring
and Evaluiation Section of KARI would undertake this function; the M & E
Section would also implement a comprehensive system of evaluation of
research projects. In order to do this, it would be necessary to compile
relevant data on agricultural commodities in different production zones
including estimated real and potential yields, benefits and production
costs. Evaluation would be mostly concerned with:
(i)   measl.ring the effect of crop/commodity and farming systems
research on production in the major production zones;
(ii)   ex-post evaluation of research projects;
(iii)   other socio-economic impact of the application of
technological innovations and adoption by farmers;
(iv)   evaluating res arch program progress.

KENYA
NATIONAL AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH PROJECT
RESEARCH PROGRAMMING CALENDAR
Date          Ac- ivity to be completed
February 1    Individual scientists and teams finalize reports on the
previous year's research and use this information as input for
making modifications in plans for current year's experiments.
1/
March 15       Programs/Centers draft their Annual Reports.
April 15       Programs/Centers draft next year's research proposals. 2/
May 1          Commodity/factor Committees and RRC scientist teams meet to
review last year's results and consider next year's propoaals.
May 15         Programs/Centers draft broad proposals for the two years after
the "next" year (to arrive at three year forward proposals
similar to the forward budget process).
June 15       Final Annual Reports and three-year draft research proposals
submitted to the KARI Planning Section.
July 15       Treasury budget guidelines communicated to MOA, MOLD and KARI.
July 31       KARI's Planning Programming and Budgeting Section submits
national program and budget (composed of Center proposals and
KARI estimates and brought in line with budget guidelines), to
KARI management which approves or modifies the plan.
1/     For centers in Central and Eastern Province these draft reports would
be completed by the end of September of the previous year in order to
be ready before the next crop season starts.
2/     For those research programs scheduled for an in-depth review by a
Specialist Committee, the period between April 15 and June 1 would be
most appropriate so as to permit the Review Report to be used in the
routine planning process.



90 -                         ANNEX II
Table 3
Page 2 of 2
August 15       Approved research programs are returned to National and Regional
Centers for development of the detailed research programs that
for most Centers will start February next.3/
September 15   Detailed research programs and budgets by commodity, factor,
discipline and Center submitted to KARI management for approval
and thereafter to the KARI Board.
January 1       Annual forward budget exercise with possible modifications of
forward budget and therefore in actual research plans.
January 15      Approval of the annual national program by KARI Board.
February 1      Final adjustments of detailed research plans on basis of last
year's results and the next - fiscal - year's budget.
February 1      Beginning of the following year's cycle.
3/ Much later (October) for the centers in Eastern and Central Provinces.

KENYA
NATIONAL AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH PROGRAM
SUGGESTED JOB DESCRIPTIONS FOR KEY KARI STAFF
INTRODUCTION
1.       Improved management of the Research Centers requires the
development of detailed job-descriptions for all research officers and
support staff working at the Center. This is ecually needed for KARI
headquarters, responsible to manage the research structure and supervise
the staff at the Centers. Clear job descriptions will indicate the
responsibility and authority of each staff member, thus helping to achieve
efficient delegation of tasks and effectiv4 supervision of results.
Ultimately, job descriptions should bp consistent and therefore one cannot
limit the job description tasks to a .ew officers. To initiate and assist
in developing these job d?scriptions, drafts are provided for some key
staff. These drafts are thp result of discussions in working groups formed
during Project preparation and descriptions already available at some
Research centers.
2.02     These job descriptions cover the following functionaries:
(i)     Director
(ii)    Deputy Director Crops, Soils and Water/Assist. Directors
(iii)   Deputy Director Livestock/Assist. Directors
(iv)    Deputy Director Finance, Planning and
Administration/Assist. Directors
(v)     Head Planning, Programming and Budgeting Section
(vi)    Head the Manpower Development and Training Section
(vii)   Principal Training Officer
(viii)  Regional Research Center Directorl
(ix)    National Research Program Coordinator
(x)     Senior Agricultural Research Officer RRC
(xi)    Researrch Officer (RRC)
(xii)   Executive Officer (RRC)
(xiii)  Research-Extension Coordinator (HQ)
I. DIRECTOR
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       The Director of KARI is the officer responsible for the
implementation of the National Agricultural Research Program in Kenya. The
Director works under the overall direction of KARI's Board of Management.
1/NRC Directors will have similar management responsibilities as RRC
Directors. However, NRC Directors will focus their research supervision
activity primarily on applied research and linkages with related Research
Institutes, while RRC Directors focus their research supervision on
adaptive research and linkages with extension.



ANNEX II
_ 94 -                    Appendix 1
Page 2 of 23
In order to fulfill this responsibility, he would spend all of his time on
issues connected to agricultural research. He would hold no other post,
nor engage in any non-research related activities. He would develop and
organize support for research at the national level. He would exercise
appropriate administrative, technical and financial control over KARI
staff, and ensure that they perform effectively. He would organize and
maintain a training program adequate to achieve a high level of
professional competence at all levels in K&RI. He would promote
satisfactory research-extension linkages and ensure an effective annual
program of field trials. He would check on the implementation of the
National Agricultural Research Program primarily through supervisory visits
to Research Centers and to farmers' fields, conveying his findings to KARI
and Ministry staff responsible and also periodically, to the Board.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The major tasks of the Director include the supervision of KARI
managers in particular the three Deputy Directors (Crops, Soils and Water,
Livestock, and Planning, Manpower Development, Finance and Administration);
participation in the activities of KARI's Board of Management; and
coordination with the Ministries of Research, Science and Technology,
Agriculture, Livestock, Plaiming, Finance, the International Research
centers, other related institutions and Donors.
3.       Critical KARI activities to be supervised by the Director include:
(i)     strategic research programming for KARI, each major
commodity factor and discipline, and for the various
Research Centers;
(ii)    preparation of the KARI Annual Research Program;
(iii)   preparation of the three-year forward budget and the
Annual Budget;
(iv)    the execution of research and its reporting;
(v)     financial management (including obtaining donor funds),
accounting, auditing, etc;
(vi)    personnel management;
(vii)   preparation and execution of training programs; and
(viii)  close coordination with research users (veterinary
department, extension service, private industry), and with
providers of basic research results (International
Agricultural Research Centers and other National
Ccenters);
The Director would also:
(i)     participate in Board of Management discussions; and



95-                          ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 3 of 23
(ii)    take part in periodic reviews of research results and
their evaluation.
QUALIFICATIONS
5.       The qualifications and experience of the Director would be:
(i)     Post-Graduate degree in agriculture;
(ii)    at least fifteen years experience in the field of
agricultural research (or exLension), preferably including
veterinary science; and
(iii)   proven ability to lead, coordinate and manage complex and
large organizations.
II. DEPUTY DIRECTOR CROPS, SOILS AND WATERIASST. DIRECTORS
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       The Deputy Director of the KARI Crops, Soils and Water Department
would have the overall management responsibility for research in each of
these areas. He would work with three Assistant Directors who he would
directly supervise. These Ore:
(i)     The Assistant Director of the Crops Division in charge of
eight National Researcii Centers including Kibos (sugar),
Lanet (seed quality), Molo (pyrethrum),, Mwea-Tebere
(cotton), Tigoni (potatoes), Thika (horticulture and
beans), Njoro (wheat oilseeds and RRC), and Kitale (maize,
fodder and pasture, and RRC);
(ii)    An Assistant Director of the Soils and Water Division in
charge of four National Research Centers which focus on
resources, factors (particularly soil and water resources)
or disciplines. These Centers cut across crop and
livestock research and include Katumani (soils and water
but also dryland farming systems and RRC); Muguga (soils
and water, plant protection, plant genetics, plant biology
and quarantine); National Agricultural Laboratories,
Nairobi (soil resources, soil survey, agricultural
chemistry, entomology, plant pathology, and research
support services); and Ahero (the National Irrigation and
Drainage Research Center) which is to be established
later; and
(iii)   An Assistant Director Regional Research Centers in charge
of five Regional Research Centers including: Embu,
Garissa, Kakamega, Kisii and Mtwapa. This Assistant
Director would also coordinate the regional research
undertaken at the three NRCs which have in addition an RRC
function (Njoro, Kitale, and Katumani). He would with the
Research/Extension Coordinator (see page 21), also be
responsible for extension liaison at headquarters, and for



-96 -                          ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 4 of 23
supervising extension liaison activities at the NRC and
RRC level.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The ma,or tasks to be supervised by the Deputy Director for Crops,
Soils and Water for the execution of which, each in their own area of
assignment, the Assistant Directors are responsible, include:
(i)     planning, management and coordination of all research
activities of the department;
(ii)    preparaticn of long term strategic rese&rch plans and
annual work programs and budgets for each of the research
programs carried out under the responsibility of the
department in close liaison with the KARI Planning,
Programming and Budgeting Section, the Monitoring and
Evaluation Section, the Deputy Director Planning, Manpower
Development, Finance and Administration, the Deputy
Director Livestock, KARI's Director and the Board;
(iii)   management ot Lhe department's expenditures and the proper
handling of all its personnel matters;
(iv)    transmission of the recommendations and decisions of the
Managing Director and the Board of Directors that concern
the department or its personnel to the Department staff;
(v)     coordination of the activities of the department with
those of the other departments of KARI and of other
organizations in and outside Kenya that carry out research
and experimentation in relevant fields;
(vi)    preparation of quarterly progress reports and annual
scientific reports for the department in close liaison
with the Monitoring and Evaluation Section, presenting
these to KARI's Managing Director and at the Annual
Research Review Conference;
(vii)   development of a training program for departmental staff
(with the Training Officer);
(viii)  determination of the department's needs in the area of
scientific documentation and the preparatic. of purchase
oriers for books and articles for transmistion to the KARI
Documentation Center;
(ix)    the department's functional relations with other
organizations (especially the Agricultural Extension
Division), related projects, farmers and other users of
research results, ensuring constant awareness of user
needs; and
(x)     compilation and presentation of the department's research
results in a form suitable for the national authorities



- 97                           ANPEX II
Appendix 1
Page 5 of 23
responsible for rural development and agricultural
research.
QUALIFICATIONS
6.       The qualifications and experience of the Deputy Director Crops,
Soils and Water would be:
(i)     a post-graduate degree in agriculture or a related field;
(ii)    at least ten years experience in relevant aspects of
agricultural research preferably related to small farm
production problems;
(iii)   actual experience in agricultural research management and
programming; and
(iv)    proven ability to lead and coordinate the activities of
multidisciplinary research teams.
7.       The qualifications and experience required for the Assistant
Directors would be similar to that for the Deputy Director except that five
years of actual research experience would be considered adequate.
III. DEPUTY DIRECTOR LIVESTOCK
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       The Deputy Director Livestock will directly supervise two
Assistant Directors in charge of National Research Centers. These are:
(i)     The Assistant Director Animal Production in charge of the
three national Livestock Research Centers including the
National Animal Production aesearch Center at Naivasha
(dairy and beef, sheep, goats, pigs ar.d poultry); the
National Range Research Center at Kiboko (range ecology,
agrometeorology, range animal production); and the Kenya
Arid Lands Research Station at Marsabit. This Assistant
Director would also be technically in charge of livestock
research at the regional research stations which are under
the Deputy Director Crops, Soil and Water.
(ii)    The Assistant Director for Animal Heaith Research in
charge of two National Veterinary Research Centers
including the National Veterinary and Animal Production
Research Center at Muguga; and the National Veterinary
Laboratories, at Kabete.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The major tasks to be supervised by the Deputy Director Livestock
and to be executed by the Assistant Directors are similar to those of the
Deputy Director in charge of Crops, Soils and Water in relation to the
specific activities of the Department (animal 9roduction and veterinary
research).



-9                         ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 6 of 23
QUALIFICATIONS
3.       The qualifications and experience of the Deputy Director for
Livestock Research would be:
(1)     a post-graduate degree in livestock, veterinary medecine
or a related field;
(ii)    at least ten years experience in relevant aspects of
livestock and/or veterinary research and knowledge of
small farm livestock production problems;
(iii)   actual experience in research management and programming;
and
(iv)    a proven ability to lead and coordinate the activities of
multidisciplinary research teams.
4.       The qualifications and experience required for the Assistant
Directors would be similar to that for the Deputy Director except that five
years of actual research experience would be considered adequate.
IV. DEPUTY DIRECTOR
FINANCE, PLANNING, AND ADMINISTRATION
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1        The Deputy Director for Planning, Manpower Development, Finance
and Administration would directly supervise three Assistant Directors;
these are:
(i)     The Assistant Director Planning and Manpower Development
in charge of four XARI headquarters Sections including (a)
the Planning, Programming and Budgetting Section which
would assist KARI management in annual programming and
budgetting, undertake medium and long range planning,
prepare commodity and factor research programs which could
be subn'tted to donors for financing and also coordinate
donor support; (b) the Monitoring and Evaluation Section
which would monitor and evaluate research undertaken at
the research centers and at the beginning of each year,
provide technical evaluations to KARI management which
together with the input from the Planning, Programming and
Budgetting Section, would enable KARI to approve (or
reject) specific research programs and projects; (c) the
Manpower Development and Training Section which would plan
the short and long term training of KARI staff, based on
the needs of research programs; and (d) the Data
Processing and Information Section;
(ii)    The Assistant Director Finance in charge of four Sections
including: (a) Accounts, (b) External Financing, (c)
Assets Management, and (d) Supplies, Procurement and
Stores; and



- 99 -                        ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 7 of 23
(iii)   The Assistant Director Administration who would manage,
six Sections including (a) Libraries, (b) Publications,
(c) Personnel Administration, (d) Station and Equipment
Maintenance, (d) New Construction, and (e) Transport.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The Deputy Director Planning, Manpowter Development, Finance and
Administration would be involved in all major KARI management decisions.
As such, he would regularly visit stations and review research results and
proposals personally. The most important tasks of the Deputy Director in
charge of Planning, Manpower Development, Finance, and Administration would
be the supervisioi. of the activities for the execution of which the
respective Assistant Directors would be responsible; these are:
(i)     research planning and programming (see job description of
Head of Planning, Programming and Budgetting Section in
collaboration with other KARI management staff and the
Board of Management;
(ii)    research monitoring and evaluation;
(iii)   training (see job description principal training officer);
(iv)    personnel management;
(v)     financial management and cost accounting;
(vi)    KARI budgeting;
(vii)   publications;
(viii)  library management;
(ix)    station and equipment management;
(x)     donor coordination and mobilization of donor funds;
(xi)    procurement.
QUALIFICATIONS
3.       The qualifications and experience of the Deputy Director Planning,
Manpower Development, Finance and Administration would be: (i) a university
degree (or its equivalent) in business administration or a related area
(ii) having formal knowledge of agricultural research, agricultural
economics and finance; and (iii) at least 10 years experience in management
and administration. The qualifications and experience of the Assistant
Directors would be similar, except for (iii): five years experience would
be considered adequate.

V. HEAD PLANNING, PROGRAMMING AND BUDGETING SECTION
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       The Head of the Planning, Programming and Budgeting Section will
carry overall responsibility for the work of tk.e Section. He will report
to the Assistant Director of the Planning and Manpower Development
Division, who in turn reports to the Deputy Director Planning, Manpower
Development, Finance and Administration.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The Head of Planning, Programming and Budgeting would be
responsible for:
(i)     planning, managing, and supervising the Planning,
Programming and Budgeting Section;
(ii)    acting as senior advisor to KARI's Managing Director
regarding the development of national systems for research
program planning, coordination, budgeting, and management;
(iii)   in coordination with the Monitoring and Evaluation
Section, and with the collaboration of the Deputy
Directors and their senior staff, evaluating research
results and updating both the annual and the long-term
agricultural research strategies;
(iv)    representing KARI management in Commodity, Factor and
Specialist Committee meetings (which develop and review
medium and long-term commodity and factor research
programs), and Center Committee meetings (which develop
research center programs);
(v)     participating in the Annual Research Conferences to review
progress with the head of the Monitoring and Evaluation
Section;
(vi)    preparation of the KARI annual research program (on the
basis of inputs from the H & E Section, Research Center
reports, proposals and publications, Commodity, Factor
Specialist and Center Committee recommendations, the
summary of the Annual Research Conference recommendations,
advice from Finance (the budget ceilings, retained
revenue, donor contributions), decisions by Management and
Board etc.);
(vii)   defense of the KARI research program and budget for
outside reviewers; and
(viii)  preparation of research sub-projects for financing by
donors.



- 101 -                      ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 9 of 23
QUALIFICATIONS
3.       The qualificatAons and experience of the Head of the Planning,
Programming and Budgeting Section would be:
(i)     a post-graduate degree in agricultural economics,
agriculture, veterinary science or a related field; and
(ii)    at least seven years experience ia agricultural research
management and programming.
VI.  HEAD MANPOWER DEVELOPMENT AND TRAINING SECTION
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       The Head of the Manpower Development and Training Section is the
officer responsible for the implementation of training programs and the
promotion of career development for all research personnel, under the
overall guidance of the Assistant Director Planning and Manpower
Development. In order to fulfill this responsibility he would develop a
strategy to lmprove and maintain a high level of professional competence of
the research staff, in consultation with appropriate Division Heads,
Research Centers Directors and external financiers. This strategy would
support priorities set and KARI's overall research framework and take into
account short as well as long-term goals. He would closely cooperate with
representatives of institutions of higher education and other research
institutes, national as well as international. He would check on the
implementation of programs through field visits to the Centers and direct
contacts with research staff, conveying his findings to KARI management and
Center Directors. He would be the primary contact point for donor funding
of research training programs.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The head of the KARI Manpower Development and Training Section
would have the following major tasks:
(i)     development and seeking management approval for annual
training programs including budgets;
(ii)'   direct supervision of the staff of the Manpower
Development and Training Section as well as consultants
assisting him in his task and reporting to him;
(iii)   ensuring that job descriptions are developed for KARI
staff in a systematic manner, discussing and updating
these with relevant staff annually and submitting these to
management; checking periodically that the training
programs remain consistent with the established and actual
job descriptions;
(iv)    ensuring that guidelines Rare prepared and updated
concerning procedures which would promote opportunities
for professional career development and upward mobility in
the research establishment;



- 102 -                    ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 10 of 23
(v)     the organization, implementati,  and evaluation of
training courses and seminars :.. Kenya;
(vi)    the progress of training and trainees abroad, by ensuring
that the context of such training responds to relevant
croplfactor/systems program objectives and stays within
budgetary limits;
(vii)   ensuring the attainment of the objectives of his section
as to the completion of the yearly training program;
(viii)  making proposals to his supervisor and KARI top management
on the organization of his section, within the context of
the general mandate of the division and KARI;
(ix)    assuring himself that the personnel section takes care of
the proper reintegration of trainees in the research
structure and programs;
(x)     receiving and evaluating trainees' reports on training
results and summarizing them in the annual report;
(xi)    if requested by the Division's Assistant Director,
representing KARI in meetings with representatives of
research and educational institutions rendering national
or international training services;
(xii)   preparing an annual report on the progress and development
of training activities and their impact on competence
improvement, development of special programs and adequacy
of center staffing;
(Yiii)  responding to t4chnical queries from external financiers
and maintaining correspondence with cooperating training
institutions;
(xiv)   preparing basic documentation and guidelines for job-
evaluation and career development; and
(xv)    preparing the yearly evaluation of the division's staff.
QUALIFICATIONS
3.       The qualifications and experience of the Head of the Manpower
Development and Training Section would be:
(i)     a post-graduate degree in agriculture or a related field;
and
(ii)    at least five years experience in the management of
training pLograms.



- 103                           ANNEX II
Appendix I

VII. PRINCIPAL TRAINING OFFICER
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       The detailed preparation and implementation of the proposed
training plan for KARI will be the responsibility of the Training Officer.
This officer would be located in KARI's Section for Manpower Development
and Training. In view of the critical importance of the training function
in KARI, the Training Officer would work directly with the Head of his
Section. The Training Officer would also work closely with senior managers
in KARI.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The functions and responsibilities of the Training Officer will
bet
(i)     to develop and review annual and periodic training plans
for KARI staff in consultation with KARI management and
the various heads of KARI Departments, Divisions and
Research Centers;
(ii)    to liaise with Nairobi University, agricultural and
veterinary colleges and other institutions in the
development of suitable training programs and courses for
scientific and technical staff of KARI;
(iii)   to compile and maintain detailed information on relevant
training programs in-country and overseas and to
periodically circulate this information in an appropriate
form to senior managers in KARI;
UiV)    to plan and organize suitable in-service training courses
for KARI staff in consultation with heads of KARI
divisions and Research Centers Directors;
(v)     to liaise with Ministry of Agriculture and with Ministry
of Livestock Departments concerning matters of training;
(vi)    to arrange periodic reviews of training courses offered to
KARI staff;
(vii)   to liaise with IARCs on matters of training, this may
require visits by the training officer to IITA, CIAT,
ICRISAT, ILCA and other Centers soon after appointment;
(viii)  to compile and maintain relevant documentation on trainees
in KARI;
(ix)    to compile annually a report on the training activities in
KARI and on progress achieved;
(x)     to assist and facilitate the preparation of training
materials for in-service training and other presentations
on training in KARI; and



ANNEX II
- 104 -                      Appendix 1
Page 12 of 23
(xi)    to establish evaluation and recording systems for training
and follow-up activities.
3.       QUALIFICATIONS
The minimum requirements for the post of Training Officer in KARI
would be:
(i)     a proven record as a competent administrator at a senior
level in large, preferably public service, organizations;
and
(ii)    a capacity to interact effectively with a diverse range of
personnel.
It would also be highly desirable, that the training officer has:
(i)     an agricultural research or agricultural education
background; and
(ii)    previous experience in managing training programs.
VIII. REGIONAL RESEARCH CENTER DIRECTOR
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       Each RRC Director will organize, manage and supervise all
activities at the RRC. The RRC Director will check on the implementation
of the RRC's entire program through supervising visits to farmers' fields,
visiting the monthly extension workshops and by conveying findings to RRC
staff and to extension staff. To do this he would spend about 20X of his
time in the field where he would visit farmers and staff in the districts
and divisions covered by the RRC. On these visits he would review the role
and impact of the field activities of the research staff, and the accuracy
and success of the transfer of research recommendations to the field. He
would communicate his findings to provincial and district extension
officers, and review, as appropriate, his suggestions for improving
operations with RRC staff. He would spend about 20X of his time in visits
to national and regional research stations and to sub-stations. He would
ensure regular visits by his research staff to farmer's fields and
participation in fortnightly extension training sessions. He would also
review the cooperation between research staff and extension staff in
organizing the monthly extension workshops, through preparation of meeting
calendars for each semester. He would monitor the timely preparation of
the program of farm trials and review (with the District Agricultural
Officers) the results of this program with District Development staff. He
would see to it that scientific resource materials required for the
implementation of the RRC program for which he is responeible are obtained
and distributed.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The functions of the RRC (as well as NRC) Directors would include:



- 105 -                     ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 13 of 23
(i)     supervising center staff and personnel management
(including the assignment of duties, staff evaluations,
assigning facilities to staff, providing professional
guidance to staff and ensuring staff well-being);
(ii)    annual research program planning, with research programs
prepared by individual researchers or teams and reviewed
by the Research Center Committee;
(iii)   monitoring and evaluation of research at the Center;
(iv)    budgeting;
(v)     overseeing fida'ncial management and accounting;
(vi)    procurement;
(vii)   station maintenance;
(viii)  station operations; and
(ix)    transmitting KARI management decisions to station staff.
3.       Because of the major new responsibilities of RRC Directors in
adaptive research, the specific tasks related to adaptive research are
listed below:
(i)     participation in studying the main agricultural production
systems in the agro-climatic zone in which the RRC is
located through diagnostic surveys and monitoring;
(ii)    coordinating and supervising adaptive research at the RRC;
(iii)   monitoring on-farm testing of research results in close
collaboration with the nationally coordinated commodity
factor and disciplinary research programs which generate
these results;
(iv)    coordinating the preparation of progress and scientific
reports on the agronomic aspects of adaptive research
according to guidelines from the Head of KARI's Monitoring
and Evaluation Section;
(v)     coordinating adaptive research activities with the
extension service of the Ministry of Agriculture and the
Ministry of Livestock Development; and
(vi)    acting as senior advisor to the diagnostic teams at the
RRC.
QUALIFICATIONS
4.       The qualifications and experience of the RRC Directors would need
to be:



- 106 -                    ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 14 of 23
(M)     a post-graduate degree in agriculture, or related field;
(ii)    at least five years experience in agricultural research,
part of which in adaptive research and preferably
experience in agricultural extension; and
(iii)   actual experience in interdisciplinary agricultural
research planning and programming.
IX. NATIONAL RESEARCH PROGRAM COORDINATOR
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       Each national commodity, factor or disciplinary research program
will have 8 program coordinator. The coordinator will be a senior
scientist capable of providing scientific leadership for the national
program. The coordinator would exercise little administrative control over
the staff of the cooperating Centers, which for all practical purposes are
an integral part of the Centers in which they are located. He must
maintain cont&cts with the Directors of the cooperating RRCs and with the
concerned scientific staff to ensure that the part of the coordinated
research program assigned to each individual is fully implemented. The
coordinators would be expected to report directly to the respective
Assistant and Deputy Director of KARI with regard to the funding of the
coordinated programs and their progress. Using the committee structure
defined in the Government's Project preparation report, the national
commmodity and factor program coordinators would organize collaborative
research programs with the appropriate NRCs and the RRCs. The Program
coordinators are responsible for convening annual Commodity or Factor
Committee meetings, preparing reports, and to act as secretary of the
Specialist Committees, in close collaboration with the relevant Deputy
Director of KARI.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       Most important tasks of the research program coordinators (in
addition to the organizational tasks described above) include:
(i)     coordinating and supervising the research activities of
all the research workers participating f '.l-time or part-
time, within or outside KARI, in the specific research
program for which the coordinator is responsible;
(ii)    coordinating execution of all relevant on-station research
work with the Station Directors;
(iii)   coordinating all laboratory services for the research
program with the chief of the central laboratories;
(iv)    preparing annual work programs and budgets, including all
central services' needs in coordination with fellow
research workers, and in close liaison with and according
to guidelines from the relevant Deputy Director;



- 107 -                        ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 15 of 23
(v)     supervising and controlling the research team's
expenditures;
(vi)    preparing quarterly progress reports and annual scientific
reports according to guidelines from KARI management;
(vii)   ensuring that research results are written up for
publication in scientific and technical journals, and are
synthesized in suitable form for the extension services;
and
(viii)  training of staff in technical and managerial matters (in
consultation with the Head Manpower Development and
Training).
3.       The qualifications and experience of a Research Program
Coordinator would be:
(i)     a post-graduate degree in agriculture, or related field;
(ii)    at least three years experience in agricultural research;
and
(iii)   a keen interest and proven ability in research management
and in leading a multidisciplinary research team.
X. SENIOR AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH OFFICER (RRC)
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       A Senior Agricultural Research Officer carries responsibility for
the execution of a research program at an RRC and leads a team of
scientists. He is responsible to the RRC Director.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The major responsibilities of a Senior Agricultural Officer would
include:
(i)     to coordinate the research program(s) allocated to station
research officers for whom he has responsibility and to
give professional and administrative guidance to these
officers;
(ii)    to formulate individual research programs with reference
to decisions made regarding overall Center research by
KARI management and the Research Center Committee;
(iii)   to advise the Center Director on all technical matters
related to research;



- 108 -                      ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 16 of 23
(iv)    to liaise with all officers under him and to formulate
seasonal and fortnightly work programs;
(v)     to assist officers under him in design, lay out, conduct,
data collection, analysis and write up of research
programs;
(vi)    to manage staff under his authority including evaluation
of their performance;
(vii)   to authorize use of research center supplies and equipment
by his team;
(viii)  to translate research findings into simple recommendations
(in consultation with the Center Director and with
extension staff) for use by farmers and extension staff;
(ix)    to keep and maintain appropriate and comprehe.'sive
registers showing all materials tested and the results;
(x)     to draw up an outline of crop/enterprise activity
schedules following a chronological order of events or
* ae other acceptable format for the purpose of giving
guidance to the Provincial and District extension staff
and the Center Director in planning for extension
activities;
(xi)    to plan and attend all exhibits used in field days and
shows and other publicity in which the Center
participates;
(xii)   to receive official visitors, farmers and other clients
visiting the Section and to keep records of such visits.
The Senior Research Officer may delegate this function
(while still retaining responsibility) to any other
officer in his Section considered competent:
(xiii)  to compile all requirements for the Section, this
includes: transport, labor, stencils, papar etc. The
stores section would be under instructions not to issue
any stores unless against a prior and approved budget;
(xiv)   to compile all research results of the Section at the end
of each season into a technical report in a style and
format prescribed by KARI;
(xv)    to ensure that all officers (senior and subordinate) are
at their respective places of work and to institute
disciplinary action (in consultation with the Center
Director) when the situation warrants it;
(xvi)   to convene at least once every fortnight, a Section
meeting in which fortnightly work plans and work progress
are discussed. Minutes of the meeting would be kept.



- 109 -                      ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 17 of 23
(xvii)  to receive new officers joining the Center and to draw up
an orientation brief (in consultation with other Section
heads);
(xviii) to participate ir the Research Center Committee when it
discusses matters pertaining to Center land use and
livestock production policy;
(xix)   to liaise (in consultation with the Center Director) with
District Extension Services to establish constraints
requiring research attention and to prioritize such
constraints; and
(xx)    to assist and encourage all others in the Section to
publish their results in scientific and other media.
QUALIFICATIONS
3.       The qualifications and experience of a Senior Agricultural
Research Officer would be:
(i)     a post-graduate degree in Agriculture or Veterinary
Science; and
(ii)    at least five years experience in conducting
interdisciplinary agricultural research.
XI. RESEARCH OFFICER (RRC)
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       The Research Officer in an RRC is the officer responsible for the
planning and implementation of research projects. In order to fulfill this
responsibility he/she would collect relevant data on which to base the
research and ensure exact implementation of program activities according to
agreed plans both in the laboratory and in the field. He/she should
generate relevant conclusions from analyses of research program results and
together with the district extension officers define recommendations for
farmers to apply on their farms. The Research Officer would report to the
Head of the Section at the RRC or research team leader as designated by the
RRC Director.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The responsibilities of a Research Officer would include:
(i)     formulation of research project(s) with reference to
decisions regarding overall center research, KARI
management and the Research Center Committee;
(ii)    design of research project(s) according to detailed
guidelines provided by KARI management. Specifically such
programs would include the following major components: (i)



- 110 -                    ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 18 of 23
title, (ii) introduction, (iii) rationale, based on
diagnostic survey. (iv) objectives/output, (v) design,
(vi) trial locations, (vii) data to be collected and
methods to be used, (ix) collaborating officers, and (x)
comprehensive budget;
(iii)   presentation and defense of proposed research program(s)
at discussions with Section Heads, Center Director and at
relevant Commodity or Factor Group meetings;
(iv)    supervision of all laboratory work and field
implementation of the program(s); provision of written
instructions to all technical and subordinate staff
carrying out data collection and other program
implementation activities. Demonstratation of the
specific tasks to be undertaken by staff and explanation
of objectives of each activity;
(v)     analysis of data and write-up of all research findings in
accordance with g4idelines provided by KARI management and
in consultation with the Section Head;
(vi)    preparation of a quarterly progress report for each
research program and description, in concise format, of
the status of program implementation;
(vii)   preparation of an end of season or final report for each
research program in accordance with the format provided by
KARI management. These reports would be finalized not
later than two months after completion of field and
laboratory work. The report would be divided into three
parts: (a) full details including raw data, (b) a
summarized version for inclusion in annual reports, and
(c) abstract form for inclusion in computerized data base
or in other forms of publication;
(viii)  interaction with extension staff through diagnostic
surveys, workshops and in the program planning and
implementation process. Being a member and attending the
relevant professional specialization group meetings.
Presenting conclusions reached at the end of each research
program, formulating field recommendations and preparing
suitable handouts jointly with extension staff;
(ix)    having continuous contact with extension staff regarding
research program implementation, participation in
extension training and other joint research-extension
related activities;
(x)     being updated on all professional aspects relevant to his
field of expertise and all allied subject matter. Being
aware of all research publications both national and
international and having personal contacts with
researchers at other Centers including IARCs; and



- 111 -                     ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 19 of 23
(xi)    participating, if appointed, to KARI Commodity and Factor
Groups as well as Specialist Committees and keeping
abreast of all their deliberations, material distributed
and conclusion reached.
The Research Officer would also:
(i)     be responsible for and directly supervise technical and
subordinate staff connected or assigned to the research
program;
(ii)    deal with all work-related correspondence within and out
of the RRC on behalf of the Director but in consultation
with the Section Head; and
(iii)   draw up his fortnightly plan of work and for technical and
subordinate staff assigned to his program.
QUALIFICATIONS
The qualifications of a Research Officer would be:
(i)     A graduate degree in agriculture or a related field; and
(ii)    proven ability in Agricultural Research.
XII. EXECUTIVE OFFICER (RRC)
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       The Executive Officer is the person responsible for assisting the
Center Director of the RRC in all areas of administration. He would be
responsible for all matters concerning personnel, budget and equipment and
all other research center administrative affairs. He would be the main
contact with KARI management on subjects pertaining to administration and
would assist the Director in supervising the implementation of GOK/KARI
managemenat administrative procedures. The fxecutive Officer would be
directly accountable to the Director of the RRC. He would represent the
Director in the coordination of RRC affairs with the Planning and Manpower
Development, Finance and Administration Divisions at KARI Headquarters.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The Executive Officer would:
(i)     deal with staff salaries (payments, increments, stoppages,
transfers and returns);
(ii)    review and update the staff list every four months at
which time he would maintain and update center complement
control and advise the Center Director of any
discrepancies;



- 112 -                         ANNEX II
Appendix 1
PaRe 20 of 23
(iii)   process and translate terms of service of all officers;
(iv)    process allowances due to all officers, draw attention of
respective officers to their allowance entitlement for
housing, leave, disturbance and others in this category;
(v)     institute all statutory deductions such as PAYE, NSSF,
NGIF;
(vi)    process and effect procedures in the event of  a
dismissal, transfer, retirement or resignation of an
officer;
(vii)   interpret COR, Ministerial, DPM, KARI management and other
similar circulars and display them on Center public notice
boards for the benefit of all officers;
(viii)  supervise administrative staff to ensure satisfactory
service. Such staff would include copy-typists, clerks,
officers of account section (through Chief Accountant),
store keepers and janitors.
(ix)    supervise proper functioning and maintenance of office
equipment and furniture;
(x)     keep record and advise KARI headquarters monthly on all
matters related to leave and overtime;
(xi)    activate the necessary GOK machinery required to board and
replace all Government stores in accordance with
Government and KARI procedures;
(xii)   assign duties and responsibilities in such a manner that
all rules and regulations governing stores are adhered to.
Carry out monthly, physical checks on stores and all
instruments of store keeping, reporting quarterly to the
Center Director. Undertake a periodical stock taking in
accordance with KARI management guidelines. Act as
supplies officer if such officer has not been appointed or
is absent;
(xiii)  prepare annual draft estimates of budget requirements in
close consultation with Section Heads and the Center
Director;
(xiv)   control all votes and submit weekly reports to the Center
Director on the status of all votes;
(xv)    maintain a serial numbered register of voucher payments.
The register would include all relevant details pertaining
to vouchers, payments or rejections;
(xvi)   prepare and examine vouchers;



- 113 -                     ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 21 of 23
(xvii) be custodian of all imprests;
(xviii) be custodian of all accounting documents;
(xix)   verify monthly expenditure returns.
(xx)    coordinate procurement of goods;
(xxi)   supervise the accounting of Appropriation in Aid (Revenue
etc.) submitting a monthly and annual report to the Center
Director;
(xxii)  receive and take appropriate action on internal and
outgoing mail coming from the Director and supervise the
taking of minutes and filing of correspondence;
(xxiii) be responsible for and maintain Center archives;
(xxiv]  be custodian of all library material and ensure the
library facilities are extended to all users; and
(xxv)   plan and be instrumental in the implementation of a
training program for officers and staff under the
Executive Officer's supervision.
QUALIFICATIONS
3.       The qualifications of an Executive Officer would be:
(i)     a graduate degree in finance and administration or a
related field; and
(ii)    at least 5 years experience in administration of
agricultural research.
XIII.  RESEARCH EXTENSION COORDINATOR (HQ)
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
1.       The Research Extension Coordinator (REC) is the officer
specifically responsible for maintaining effective cooperation between
research and extension staff. In order to fulfill this responsibility, he
would spend all his time intensifying research/extension linkages. The REC
would hold no other post, nor engage in activities not related to research-
extension coordination. He would develop and organize meetings and
seminars at the national level to improve cross-fertilization of ideas
emanating from the research and extension systems. He would identify,
organize and promote training programs adequate to maintain the
professional skills of the research staff, so as to enable them to respond
to the demand for information generated by the extension program. He would
check on the implementation of the program through visits to farmers'
fields, monthly workshops and Research Centers, conveying his findings to



- 114 -                      ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 22 of 23
the relevant Research Centers and extension staff. The REC would report to
the Assistant Director RRCs of KARI and coordinate with the Chief
Agricultural Extension, Services and Administration of MOA.
MAJOR TASKS
2.       The REC would:
(i)     spend about 301 of his time in the field where he would
visit farmers and research and extension staff. On these
visits he would review the role and impact of the field
activities of the research staff and the accuracy and
success of the transfer of research recommendations to the
field. He would communicate his findings to provincial
and district extension officers, and review as appropriate
his suggestions for improving operations with the relevant
research staff;
(ii)    spend about 30X of his time on visits to national and
regional Research Centers and to sub-centres. On these
visits he would review with station staffs (a) how best to
respond to problems identified by the extension program;
and (b) the possible consequences of these problems for
future research programming and budgeting;
(iii)   ensure visits by research and extension staff to frmers'
fields and the participation of research staff in monthly
workshops and professional specialization group
activities. He would also review the participation of
research staff in organizing the monthly workshops,
through preparation of meeting calendars for each
semester. He would see to it that researchers, teaching
at the monthly workshops, would be trained (as required)
in didactical skills;
(iv)    through meetings such as those of the PAREAC, professional
specialization groups, monthly workshops, and individually
with researchers, facilitate the proper functioning of the
joint research/extension on-farm trials and review with
KARI and extension management the results of this program;
(v)     review the physical and financial requirements of the
research/extension liaison activities and ensure that
allocations received by the Center Directors are used
correctly and in a timely fashion. For this purpose he
would liaise closely with District, Provincial and Central
Agricultural Officers;
(vi)    see that scientifHc resource material required for the
implementation of the program are obtained and distributed
as needed;
(vii)   participate regularly and represent KARI in all meetings
of National, Provincial and District extension staff.



- 115 -                     ANNEX II
Appendix 1
Page 23 of 23
(viii)  see to it that the RRC would include in the draft annual
report the functioning and effectiveness of
research/extension interaction;
(ix)    react to responsible officers on reports analyzing the
results of on-farm trials and on extension renitoring and
evaluation reports, as appropriate; and
(x)     inform Research Centers Directors about important research
questions generated by the extension program.
QUALIFICATIONS
3.       The qualifications of the Research Extension Coordinator would be:
(i)     a post-graduate degree in agriculture or a related field;
(ii)    at least five years experience in agricultural research;
and
(iii)   at least five years experience in agricultural extension.

KENYA
NATIONAL AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH PROJECT
THE PLAN OF ACTION
The implementation of NARP requires numerous actions at specific
dates. To ensure the effective execution of Project activities, several of
these actions need to then go on continuously or be repeated on a monthly,
seasonal or annual basis. The most critical of these have been summarized
below; the relevant para(4) in the Staff Appraisal Report are indicated in
parentheses. The implementation schedule of actions to be taken by KARI,
its subdivisions and other organizations has also been illustrated in a
bar chart (pages 5-7). Except for those actions and dates specifically
referred to in the legal agreements between IDA, GOK and KARI, target dates
and timings are indicative; they would be reviewed and if necessary revised
at the times of the annual joint donor reviews of the NARP.

1/     These indicators would be used as rough guides in helping to set research priorities.  During Project implementation, KARI's Planning Division
would elaborate on these guidelines for use in helping to adjust research priorities and the allocation of NARP funds. Since KARI is not
responsible for coffee and tea research, the figures exclude these two commodities.
2/     Source of data Is from GOK's Sessional Paper No. 1, 1986. Values refer to the year 1983/84.
3/     Initially the criteria (i.e. good, average, poor) for these two indicators will be based on a somewhat subjective judgment, taking into account
future supply and demand trends likely to face Kenya; further quantification of these indicators by KARl during Project implementation could serve
as a useful guide for assessing Kenya's prospects for food security, export earnings and import substitution.
4/     Includes range land production.
S/     A distinction shouid be made between high and medium potential areas and cropped dryland areas.
3/     For livestock activities, the indicators of land area, farmgate value and employment have limited meaning.
7/     It is not possible to, in a meaningful manner, relate the indicators to NARP costs of other major research programs such as: soil and water: Kt8.3
million (6.7X); veterinary: KL28.4 million (19.51); and range and arid lands, Kk11.1 million (7.6%).



- 139 -
ANNEX V
Table 2
KENYA
NATIONAL AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH PROJECT
MAIN CONSIDERATIONS IN SETTING RESEARCH PRIORITIES 1
(i)     The economic -- and social as well as political --
importance of a commodity or region (i.e. current or
potential contribution to agricultural GDP, employment,
farmer incomes, nutrition, etc.). Relevant data are: area
involved, potential production, numbers of people to
benefit, employment projections, impact on foreign
exchange earnings and savings.
(ii)    Current market demand for particular commodities and
future projections. Indicative data for food crops
include: population pressure, changes in land use, price
treads, trade projections and changes in consumption
patterns. For industrial crops: changing demands for
export and local transformation (e.g. textile processing).
(iii)   The chances of a successful outcome of the research.  This
implies a highly subjective assessment of scientific
probabilities, time scales, resources needed, and probable
costs and benefits. Past experience and current knowledge
would be guiding factors.
(iv)    The factors which may affect adoption of results.  This
involves assessments of: the needs and perceptions (risk,
cost, etc.) of clients, the effectiveness of supporting
services, the level of political commitment, and the
possibility of policy-imposed constraints, e.g. pricing,
import policies, market quotas, etc.
(v)     The probable distribution of benefits from research.  This
involves a careful analysis of equity/efficiency,
producer/consumer, and other interests.
l/Taken from a paper prepared by a Working Group of the Special Program for
African Agricultural Research, "Guidelines for Strengthening National
Agricultural Research Systems in Sub Sahara Africa" (draft, October 1986).
There are at least five general considerations to take into account in
assessing what priorities and how many resources to allocate to a
particular commodity or group of commodities. KARI's Planning Division
would seek to apply these considerations in setting and adjusting its
research priorities and allocating its funds.

KENYA
National Agricultural Research Project
SELECTED DOCUMENTS AND DATA AVAILABLE IN THE PROJECT PILE
A.       Sector/Subsector Reports and Studies
1.   Kenya's National Agricultural Research System, ISNAR, The
Hague, September 1981.
2.   Kenya Agricultural Research Strategy and Plan, ISNAR, The
Hague, December 1985, 2 volumes.
3.   Kenya National Agricultural Research Project Working Papers,
prepared by the Joint-Donor Mission, July 1986.
4.   Kenya National Agricultural Research Program Joint-Donor
Mission Evaluation Report, February 1987.
5.   GOK Sessional Paper No. 1 of 1986.  Economic Management for
Renewed Growth.
6.   Science and Technology Act of 1977, (amended) in 1979.
7.   State Corporations Act of 1986.
B.       Project Related Reports and Studies
1.   National Agricultural Research Project Proposal (Draft) in
two volumes, April 1986.
2.   National Agricultural Research Program, Preparation Report,
Ministry of Agriculture, September 24, 1986.
2.   Kenya, Agricultural Inputs Study, Report IBRD 5643-KE, June
10, 1985, 3 volumes.
3.   Kenya, National Seed Quality Control Service, Evaluation
report on Netherlands Assistance, March 1983.
C.       Implementation Related Documents
1.   Consultant's Report on Livestock by K. Meyn, April 1987.
2.   Consultant's Report on KARI Research Information Systems by
S. Akwera, April 1987.
3.   Consultant's Report on Laboratory and other Equipment by W.F.
Pieters, April 1987.
4.   Consultant's Report on Civil Works by G. Jenkinson, April
1987.
